2026-05-17T00:23:50.6706037Z   Program Headers:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6706371Z     LOAD       off=0x000000 vaddr=0x00400000 filesz=8192   memsz=8192   flags=RX align=0x1000
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6706886Z     LOAD       off=0x003000 vaddr=0x00403000 filesz=512    memsz=1024   flags=RW align=0x1000

2026-05-17T00:23:50.6709144Z     .text              PROGBITS   addr=0x00401000 off=0x1000 size=4096   flags=AX
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6709550Z     .rodata            PROGBITS   addr=0x00402000 off=0x2000 size=256    flags=A
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6709969Z     .data              PROGBITS   addr=0x00403000 off=0x3000 size=512    flags=WA
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6710582Z     .bss               NOBITS     addr=0x00403200 off=0x3200 size=512    flags=WA
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6710956Z     .symtab            SYMTAB     addr=0x00000000 off=0x3200 size=384    flags=
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6711331Z     .strtab            STRTAB     addr=0x00000000 off=0x3380 size=128    flags=
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6711697Z     .shstrtab          STRTAB     addr=0x00000000 off=0x3400 size=64     flags=
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6712168Z     Note: .bss is NOBITS — takes no space in file, zero-filled in memory
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6712670Z     Note: .symtab/.strtab have vaddr=0 — not loaded, tools read from file
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6712929Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6713050Z 3. Section → Segment mapping:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.6713300Z    PT_LOAD (R+X): .text, .rodata  (code segment)

2026-05-17T00:23:50.8785247Z   -----          ------ ----
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8785566Z   e_ident             0   16
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8785910Z   e_type             16    2
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8786218Z   e_machine          18    2
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8786518Z   e_version          20    4
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8786821Z   e_entry            24    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8787167Z   e_phoff            32    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8788013Z   e_shoff            40    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8788445Z   e_flags            48    4
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8788838Z   e_ehsize           52    2
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8789048Z   e_phentsize        54    2

2026-05-17T00:23:50.8789424Z   e_shentsize        58    2
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8789614Z   e_shnum            60    2
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8789800Z   e_shstrndx         62    2

2026-05-17T00:23:50.8790052Z 2. Program header (Elf64_Phdr):
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8790267Z   sizeof(Elf64_Phdr) = 56 bytes
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8790475Z   Field        Offset Size
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8790676Z   -----        ------ ----
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8791104Z   p_type            0    4
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8791289Z   p_flags           4    4
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8791474Z   p_offset          8    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8791655Z   p_vaddr          16    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8791831Z   p_paddr          24    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8792014Z   p_filesz         32    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8792193Z   p_memsz          40    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8792379Z   p_align          48    8
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8792493Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8792569Z 3. Section header (Elf64_Shdr):
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8792775Z   sizeof(Elf64_Shdr) = 64 bytes
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8792902Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8793002Z 4. Segment types (program header p_type):
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8793267Z   0x00000000  PT_NULL         Unused entry
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8793604Z   0x00000001  PT_LOAD         Loadable segment (mapped by kernel)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8793984Z   0x00000002  PT_DYNAMIC      Dynamic linking info (.dynamic section)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8794339Z   0x00000003  PT_INTERP       Path to dynamic linker
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8794696Z   0x00000004  PT_NOTE         Auxiliary info (build-id, ABI version)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8795051Z   0x00000006  PT_PHDR         Program header table itself
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8795402Z   0x6474e551  PT_GNU_STACK    Stack permissions (NX enforcement)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8795757Z   0x6474e552  PT_GNU_RELRO    Read-only after relocation
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8795955Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8796050Z 5. Standard ELF sections:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8796270Z   Section        Type   Flags Description
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8796526Z   -------        ----   ----- -----------
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8796770Z   .text          1      AX    Executable code
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8797110Z   .rodata        1      A     Read-only data
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8797679Z   .data          1      AW    Initialized read-write data
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8798165Z   .bss           8      AW    Uninitialized data (no file space)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8798611Z   .symtab        2      -     Symbol table
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8799054Z   .strtab        3      -     String table (symbol names)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8799524Z   .shstrtab      3      -     Section name string table
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8799994Z   .rela.text     4      -     Relocations for .text
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8800532Z   .dynamic       6      AW    Dynamic linking info
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8801169Z   .note          7      A     Build metadata (build-id)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8801858Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8801966Z 6. Building a minimal ELF64 binary in memory:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8802250Z   Generated 120 bytes (header + 1 program header)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8802512Z   Magic: 7f ELF
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8802711Z   Class: 2 (64-bit), Data: 1 (little-endian)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8802947Z   Type:    2 (ET_EXEC)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8803140Z   Machine: 0x3e (EM_X86_64)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8803332Z   Entry:   0x401000
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8803529Z   PhOff:   64 (program headers at byte 64)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8803774Z   PhNum:   1 program header(s)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8804032Z   Segment: PT_LOAD, r-x, vaddr=0x401000, align=0x1000
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8804230Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8804307Z 7. Section vs segment duality:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8804540Z   Sections (.text, .data, .bss) = linker's view
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8804802Z     - Organize code and data by type
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8805069Z     - Used for symbol resolution, relocation, linking
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8805388Z     - Optional for execution (strip -s removes them)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8805593Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8805676Z   Segments (PT_LOAD) = loader's view
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8805934Z     - Describe memory mappings with permissions
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8806219Z     - Multiple sections map into one segment:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8806581Z       .text + .rodata → PT_LOAD (r-x)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8806845Z       .data + .bss   → PT_LOAD (rw-)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8807092Z     - Required for execution (kernel reads these)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8807487Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8807643Z 8. Common ELF machine types:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8808000Z   0x003e  EM_X86_64 (AMD64)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8808211Z   0x00b7  EM_AARCH64 (ARM 64-bit)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8808582Z   0x00f3  EM_RISCV (RISC-V)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8808779Z   0x0003  EM_386 (x86 32-bit)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8808977Z   0x0028  EM_ARM (ARM 32-bit)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8809107Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8809297Z 9. .bss section — zero-initialized, no file space:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8809692Z   .bss has SHT_NOBITS type — no bytes stored in the ELF file.
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8810027Z   The loader allocates MemSz bytes and zeros them.
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8810315Z   This is why FileSz < MemSz for the data segment:
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8810566Z     FileSz covers .data only
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8810776Z     MemSz  covers .data + .bss
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8811078Z   A 1GB zero-initialized array adds 0 bytes to the file.
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8811431Z   Example: FileSz=256, MemSz=4352, .bss=4096 bytes (zero-filled)
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8811655Z 
2026-05-17T00:23:50.8811765Z All ELF and executable format examples passed.

2026-05-17T00:24:24.5722972Z   0x40 — bare REX (no extensions)

2026-05-17T00:24:24.5724156Z   0x49 — REX.WB (64-bit + extended r/m)

2026-05-17T00:24:24.5724903Z 
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5725023Z 2. ModR/M byte: [mod:2][reg:3][r/m:3]
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5725409Z   0xc0 — mod=11, reg=rax, r/m=rax
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5725751Z   0xc8 — mod=11, reg=rcx, r/m=rax
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5726064Z   0xc1 — mod=11, reg=rax, r/m=rcx
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5726380Z   0x05 — mod=00, reg=rax, r/m=101 (RIP-relative!)
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5726705Z   0x45 — mod=01, reg=rax, r/m=rbp (disp8)
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5726992Z   Note: mod=00, r/m=101 is RIP-relative, NOT [RBP]!
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5727554Z   To encode [RBP], use mod=01 with disp8=0x00.

2026-05-17T00:24:24.5735496Z   Prefer shorter encodings for better I-cache utilization:
2026-05-17T00:24:24.5735712Z

2026-05-17T00:26:47.9890412Z

2026-05-17T00:27:21.6819803Z       read = 0

2026-05-17T00:27:21.6821012Z     getpid = 39
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6821257Z       exit = 60
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6821403Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6821698Z 2. Register mapping — syscall vs function call:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6822184Z     Arg    Syscall   Function
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6822627Z     ---    -------   --------
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6823031Z       1        rdi        rdi
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6823452Z       2        rsi        rsi
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6823762Z       3        rdx        rdx
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6823993Z       4        r10        rcx ←
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6824193Z       5         r8         r8
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6824380Z       6         r9         r9
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6824630Z   (← marks where they differ: 4th arg)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6824795Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6824888Z 3. SYSCALL instruction side effects:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6825186Z   Before SYSCALL executes, the CPU automatically:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6825530Z     RCX ← RIP  (return address saved in RCX)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6825837Z     R11 ← RFLAGS  (flags saved in R11)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6826153Z   After SYSRET, the kernel restores RIP from RCX and RFLAGS from R11.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6826538Z   Consequence: any value you had in RCX or R11 is destroyed.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6826894Z   This is why the 4th syscall arg uses R10 instead of RCX.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6827098Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6827222Z 4. Raw syscalls via ctypes (libc's syscall() wrapper):
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6827730Z   getpid via syscall(39): 19556
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6827948Z   getpid via os.getpid():    19556
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6828234Z   PIDs match — same underlying syscall.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6828510Z   Hello from raw syscall via ctypes!
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6828747Z   write returned: 37 bytes (expected 37)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6829017Z   write(fd=999) returned: -1, errno: 9 (EBADF=9)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6829225Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6829400Z 5. os module — Python's high-level syscall wrappers:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6829689Z   os.getpid() = 19556
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6829887Z   Hello from os.write()!
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6830095Z   os.write(1, ...) wrote 25 bytes
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6830318Z   os.uname().sysname  = Linux
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6830529Z   os.uname().machine  = x86_64
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6830665Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6831086Z 6. Syscall cost — why buffering matters:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6833480Z   A syscall (user→kernel transition) costs ~100-300 CPU cycles.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6833875Z   A function call costs ~3-5 cycles.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6834272Z   Writing 4096 bytes one byte at a time = 4096 syscalls = ~1.2M cycles.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6834870Z   Writing 4096 bytes in one call = 1 syscall = ~600 cycles.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6835400Z   Python's print() buffers internally to amortize this cost.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6835970Z   os.write() does NOT buffer — it's one syscall per call.
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6836504Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6836598Z 7. Key takeaways:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6836958Z   - Syscall nr in RAX, args in RDI,RSI,RDX,R10,R8,R9, return in RAX
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6837660Z   - SYSCALL clobbers RCX (←RIP) and R11 (←RFLAGS)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6837973Z   - 4th arg is R10 for syscalls, RCX for function calls
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6838323Z   - Negative returns in [-4095,-1] are errors (negate for errno)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6838737Z   - Minimize syscall count on hot paths — buffer I/O
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6839046Z >>> OUTPUT_END syscalls_and_abi/Python (exit=0)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6839327Z   ✓ Python
2026-05-17T00:27:21.6839544Z >>> END_TEST topic=syscalls_and_abi lang=Python rc=0

2026-05-17T00:27:21.7405441Z 6. Key facts:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.7405719Z   - SYSCALL clobbers RCX (saves RIP) and R11 (saves RFLAGS)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.7406063Z   - Negative return in [-4095,-1] = error (negate for errno)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.7406374Z   - Stack must be 16-byte aligned before CALL
2026-05-17T00:27:21.7406669Z   - Structs >16 bytes returned via hidden pointer in RDI
2026-05-17T00:27:21.7406995Z   - Red zone: 128 bytes below RSP usable by leaf functions

2026-05-17T00:27:21.8545207Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8545284Z 3. RawSyscall vs Syscall:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8545477Z   syscall.Syscall:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8545720Z     - Notifies Go scheduler before/after kernel entry
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8546041Z     - Allows goroutine preemption and GC cooperation
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8546387Z     - Safe for potentially blocking syscalls (read, write, etc.)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8546708Z   syscall.RawSyscall:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8547015Z     - No scheduler notification — faster but dangerous
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8547586Z     - Blocks the entire OS thread (other goroutines stall)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8547948Z     - Only safe for non-blocking syscalls (getpid, getuid, etc.)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8548280Z   RawSyscall(getpid) = 19639 (matches: true)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8548460Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8548561Z 4. Go's internal ABI vs System V AMD64:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8548825Z   System V AMD64 (C, Rust, etc.):
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8549057Z     Args: RDI, RSI, RDX, RCX, R8, R9
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8549280Z     Return: RAX
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8549473Z     Callee-saved: RBX, RBP, R12-R15
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8549625Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8549710Z   Go register ABI (since Go 1.17):
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8549965Z     Integer args: RAX, RBX, RCX, RDI, RSI, R8-R11
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8550262Z     Integer returns: RAX, RBX, RCX, RDI, RSI, R8-R11
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8550545Z     Different order, different set of registers
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8550723Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8550809Z   Key differences:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8551039Z     - Go uses its own register assignment (not System V)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8551386Z     - Go goroutine stacks start small (2-8KB) and grow dynamically
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8551756Z     - Go inserts stack-growth checks at function entry (preamble)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8552133Z     - For cgo calls, Go switches to a C-sized stack and uses System V
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8552532Z     - For syscalls, Go's runtime loads the kernel ABI registers directly
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8552774Z 
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8552859Z 5. Kernel syscall register mapping:
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8553092Z   Arg      Syscall    Function(C)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8553307Z   ---      -------    -----------
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8553647Z   1        rdi        rdi       
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8553990Z   2        rsi        rsi       
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8554334Z   3        rdx        rdx       
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8554636Z   4        r10        rcx        <-
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8554956Z   5        r8         r8        
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8555261Z   6        r9         r9        
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8555659Z   (<- 4th arg differs: R10 for syscall, RCX for function call)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8556190Z   SYSCALL clobbers RCX (saves RIP) and R11 (saves RFLAGS)
2026-05-17T00:27:21.8556521Z
